  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a3da740f-db8e-451b-87d1-ac2cfc87eb00'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText13171015965389512780" style="display:none"><i>"One thing my mother never knew, and would disapprove of most of all, was that I watched the Garretts. All the time."</i><br /><br />The Garretts are everything the Reeds are not. Loud, messy, affectionate. And every day from her rooftop perch, Samantha Reed wishes she was one of them . . . until one summer evening, Jase Garrett climbs up next to her and changes everything.<br /><br />As the two fall fiercely for each other, stumbling through the awkwardness and awesomeness of first love, Jase's family embraces Samantha - even as she keeps him a secret from her own. Then something unthinkable happens, and the bottom drops out of Samantha's world. She's suddenly faced with an impossible decision. Which perfect family will save her? Or is it time she saved herself?<br /><br />A transporting debut about family, friendship, first romance, and how to be true to one person you love without betraying another.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10651981204101573761"><br/><b>What I loved about this book:</b><br/>1. <b>NO</b> teenage angst from Samantha<br/>2. <b>NO</b> teenage drama with the main characters<br/>3. Jase and Samantha were very mature 17-year-olds (very refreshing)<br/>4. <b>GEORGE</b><br/>5. The Garrett family<br/>6. The easy, loving, trusting and patient relationship Jase has with Samantha <br/>7. I <b>LOVED</b> that this book put a smile on my face and made me laugh almost the entire book. Although it did have me teary eye a little bit at one point. :o)<br/>8. <b>FINALLY</b> I loved that this book sucked me in and never wanted</span>
  <span id="freeText10651981204101573761" style="display:none"><br /><b>What I loved about this book:</b><br />1. <b>NO</b> teenage angst from Samantha<br />2. <b>NO</b> teenage drama with the main characters<br />3. Jase and Samantha were very mature 17-year-olds (very refreshing)<br />4. <b>GEORGE</b><br />5. The Garrett family<br />6. The easy, loving, trusting and patient relationship Jase has with Samantha <br />7. I <b>LOVED</b> that this book put a smile on my face and made me laugh almost the entire book. Although it did have me teary eye a little bit at one point. :o)<br />8. <b>FINALLY</b> I loved that this book sucked me in and never wanted me to put it down.<br /><br />Samantha lives next door to Jase for 10 years before they actually have their first encounter with each other on a face-to-face level. She's from a well to do family and he's from a family of 8 children and a crazy/loud household. His family is something she wishes she could be a part of while her family is "prim and proper", mostly, and she always follows the rules. When Jase comes in to the picture it literally turns her world upside down. <br /><br />This summer Samantha will fall in love and she will find the courage and strength to stand up for her self. She will also learn the importance of friendship, family, love, and making the right choices. Ultimately she will learn that no matter the price you have to sacrifice by telling the truth, even if you lose what you love the most, that some people are willing to stick by you no matter what, all you have to do is give them a chance. <br /><br /><b> FAVORITE SCENE with George, Samantha and Jase:</b><br />"Is Jase already going to marry you?"<br />I start coughing again. "Uh. No. No, George. I'm only seventeen." As if that's the only reason we aren't engaged.<br />"I'm this many," George holds up four slightly grubby fingers. "Jase is seventeen and a half. You could. Then you could live in here with him. And have a big family." <br />Jase strides back into the room, of course, midway through this proposition. "George. Beat it. Discovery Channel is on."<br />George backs out of the room, but not before saying, "His bed's really comfortable. And he never pees in it."<br />The door closes and we both start laughing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10651981204101573761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229655108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229655108" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229655108?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=sweet-romance">sweet-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=next-door">next-door</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229655108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11280492699555939193"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/huntley-fitzpatrick/review-my-life-next-door.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362248i/713384.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This is why I read YA books - to get this feeling of joy, of happiness, of love.. Because I simply <em>LOVE</em> feeling my head so light and having my heart skip a beat remembering how it felt to fall in love for the first time (and every time after that).<br/><br/>I really like stories like this, that get you through every stage of a young relationship; that make you hold your breath for the romantic moments, for the first kiss; that make you smile at all the silliness and cuteness of the couple; that make y</span>
  <span id="freeText11280492699555939193" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/huntley-fitzpatrick/review-my-life-next-door.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362248i/713384.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is why I read YA books - to get this feeling of joy, of happiness, of love.. Because I simply <em>LOVE</em> feeling my head so light and having my heart skip a beat remembering how it felt to fall in love for the first time (and every time after that).<br><br>I really like stories like this, that get you through every stage of a young relationship; that make you hold your breath for the romantic moments, for the first kiss; that make you smile at all the silliness and cuteness of the couple; that make you ache for them when they are in trouble and fall apart; that make you love them more when they get back together, much stronger as a couple, much more in love, knowing themselves better, accepting each other with the good and the bad, feeling their love grow with every page, with every word...<br><br>I guess what I mean is that this is a very sweet romantic story that went straight to my heart and doesn't plan to leave too soon!<br>There were so many emotions radiating through these pages, with all that drama and those tangled situations that I almost didn't see a way to end the story well. It was all so full of substance - there was so much to laugh about, to smile about, to care about... So much to enjoy, so much to love.<br><br>And yes, the romance is absolutely lovely: This is how first love feels like: a bit clumsy, out of place, unpredictable (and supposedly world-shattering), but also damn cute. It made me smile, scratch that, it made me giggle like a child. I like their sweetness and their cuteness and i could savor this love-story forever.<br><br>The characters were amazing as well.<br><br>I loved the main character, <strong>Samantha</strong>. There was something about her dreamy way of beeing, about the way she thought about and watched from afar the family next door so opposed to her own, the way she started to feel so loved by some people that she barely knew, the way she needed to live for once after all that <em>watching-other-people-live-their-lives</em> thing she's been doing.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/huntley-fitzpatrick/review-my-life-next-door.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362248i/713385.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Also, I liked how she always wanted to help, how she worked even though she didn't need to, how she tried to stick to the truth even thoug it was supposed to break her.<br>I am not sure what would i have done in her place. I love my family and I guess i would stick to them no matter what, but I definitely hope not to find out this on my own.<br><br>Then we have <strong>Jace</strong>.<br>He was the best first boyfriend you could have. Smart, cute, funny, and patient. I liked how open he was and honest, how he treated Sam so well even when things got rough. Also I loved how he was there for his siblings, for his parents, and I loved how he kept fighting for his dreams (figuratively speaking) even though there were such slim chances for them to come true.<br>There's only one thing that I missed - I wanted him to play a song for Sam, as i love guys paying guitar.<br><br>My favorite character is probably little <strong>George</strong>. I mean, how could you not love him? He is the cutest boy ever!! He is smart and sweet and so damn lovely; I wanted to kiss him, to hug him, to take him home and adopt him. He made me laugh so damn much and he deserves all the love and the fans he can get.<br><br>And as we're still at it, there was one more character that I loved -  <strong>Tim.</strong><br>He was troubled, but he was such a nice guy. I didn't know he was supposed to have so much impact in this story, so it was a great surprise and I loved all the moments with him. He was such a good friend (when he was not being a jerk and when he was sober).<br><br>This brings me somehow back to his sister, <em>Nan</em> - the very opposite of him. We didn't get to know how things eneded with her, but things like this happen all the time. You have friends until one day you don't have them anymore.<br>Things like 'best friends forever' are easier to say than do, and the truth is that you don't need to <em>work</em> on keeping close a friend, you just have to be there, to enjoy the friendship.<br><br>This being said, this book was awesome. I loved it and i can't wait to read more from this author. I still wonder what would I do in Sam's shoes. I am definitely not sure.<br>I know that when you fall in love you think that you deserve happiness (and you probably do), and when something so dark comes upon your love you need to have all the luck on your side to make things right again. Again not sure if this was the way to do it. I agree that these things can be handled privately - scandals and fights are so not my thing, but anyways it is a shame that someone might need to get to something like that, that someone might suffer (not only one person, but many more; not only one family, but two).<br><br>So, let's welcome Huntley Fitzpatrick in this fabulous world of books!<br>I really can't wait for more awesomeness written by her, so...<br>Happy writing Huntley and happy reading you guys!<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/huntley-fitzpatrick/review-my-life-next-door.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339972i/696540.jpg" alt="" width="483" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i> ** For a better visual effect, read this review at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/huntley-fitzpatrick/review-my-life-next-door.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a> </i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11280492699555939193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_533424066" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/533424066" />
    <a title="Liz* Fashionably Late" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8191214-liz-fashionably-late"><img alt="Liz* Fashionably Late" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385594860p2/8191214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/533424066?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz* Fashionably Late" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz* Fashionably Late" href="/user/show/8191214-liz-fashionably-late">Liz* Fashionably Late</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=sexy-times">sexy-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=the-shelf-of-shame">the-shelf-of-shame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=young-adults">young-adults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=kill-it-with-fire">kill-it-with-fire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=it-could-be-worse">it-could-be-worse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=fooled-by-the-cover">fooled-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8191214-liz-fashionably-late?shelf=drama-queen">drama-queen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer533424066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14505120384652597531"><br/><b>UNPOPULAR OPINION HERE. </b><br/><br/>Samantha is a rich, <b>perfect</b> girl with the <b>perfect</b> life, body and shit. She's got it all but a boyfriend. Her neighbor is single, hot and <b>ridiculously perfect.</b> She's been <s>stalking</s> admiring him from her balcony for evah. HEY, IT'S LIKE MEANT TO BE. The thing is Mom hates the Garrets. They're too many (eight kids) and those morons never heard about birth control so Sam will be in SERIOUS trouble if she fraternizes with the enemy.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395747847ra/9039114.gif' width='230' height='160' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/>Life won't give her a break, though. She is s</span>
  <span id="freeText14505120384652597531" style="display:none"><br><b>UNPOPULAR OPINION HERE. </b><br><br>Samantha is a rich, <b>perfect</b> girl with the <b>perfect</b> life, body and shit. She's got it all but a boyfriend. Her neighbor is single, hot and <b>ridiculously perfect.</b> She's been <s>stalking</s> admiring him from her balcony for evah. HEY, IT'S LIKE MEANT TO BE. The thing is Mom hates the Garrets. They're too many (eight kids) and those morons never heard about birth control so Sam will be in SERIOUS trouble if she fraternizes with the enemy.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395747847ra/9039114.gif" width="230" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Life won't give her a break, though. She is surrounded by cheaters, liars, addicts, so it's no wonder she secretly hangs out with the Garrets. <b>EVERYONE around Sam is corrupt, mean and a bad influence but her.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395747847ra/9039114.gif" width="230" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mom works all the time, Sam is usually alone so one day Jace pulls an Edward Cullen, climbs up to Samantha's balcony and BOOM, Cupid! They fall in love. I'd call it instalove but she's been stalking him for years, so...<br><br>Life is good. Sam works, Jase works. Everybody works but wait... Tim and Nan: the fucked up siblings. Nan turns out to be a cheater, envious of Sam's great accomplishments and perfect boyfriend. But Nan's tired of her life, college is going to be her ticket out because she has her conflicts too, right? I'm sure Sam wants to know why her friend is so confused and why she needs to run away so desperately but wait... WHY IS NAN CHEATING? WHY WOULD NAN DO THIS TO SAM? <b>IT'S SO UNFAIR FOR PERFECT SAM!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395747847ra/9039114.gif" width="230" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aaaand there's Tim. He's your typical bad boy character. A lot of swearing and smoking.<b> And swearing too. </b>And apparently, TIM IS FUCKING HONEST, FOR FUCK SAKE. FUCK. <br><br>So after being fucking angry (that scene was so stupid), he quit his immoral job.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395747847ra/9039114.gif" width="230" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I dislike so many more things about this book:<br><br>I dislike this weird dynamic between Jase, Sam and Tim. And at one point, I just couldn't care any less to understand. <br><br>I dislike sweet, forgiving George. Dude, YOU NEED TO STOP TALKING (This book makes me hate a little kid. This book is evil.)<br><br>I dislike Samantha's mom. Obviously. That control-freak bitch.<br><br>I dislike the fact that almost <b>nothing happened and so many issues were left unsolved.</b><br><br>I dislike the fact that <b>the "unexpected event" was so obviously implemented there</b> with no connection whatsoever with the story line, just to try to mix things up a little. And the ending was so perfectly convenient for everybody I still feel like throwing up. <br><br>I dislike the beautiful, deceptive cover.<br><br>I dislike all the expectations I had when I started reading this book.<br><br>I dislike the fact that I'm the only one who dislikes this book.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14505120384652597531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText623833554763024072" style="display:none">When I checked this book out at the library, my favorite librarian looked at me funny and said "This is not a you book". For years. <br>Then she finally gets to meet one of them. Jace. <div id="review_840337774" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/840337774" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/840337774?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer840337774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11061648406609681621">You know how I'm a contemporary snob? And it takes sooooo muuuuch for a contemporary to wrap around my heart and turn me into happiness and sprinkles? <b>Well this book successfully stole my heart.</b> SCRAP THAT. IT STOLE MY SOUL. I AM SO IMPRESSED RIGHT NOW. I have a few niggles, but gahhhhhh. I <i>loved</i> it. It basically went through a checklist of ALL the things that win me over. So it's basically possible that Huntley Fitzpatrick wrote it <i>for</i> me, okay? Just so you know. <br/><br/>Because it had:<br/>• huge emphasis </span>
  <span id="freeText11061648406609681621" style="display:none">You know how I'm a contemporary snob? And it takes sooooo muuuuch for a contemporary to wrap around my heart and turn me into happiness and sprinkles? <b>Well this book successfully stole my heart.</b> SCRAP THAT. IT STOLE MY SOUL. I AM SO IMPRESSED RIGHT NOW. I have a few niggles, but gahhhhhh. I <i>loved</i> it. It basically went through a checklist of ALL the things that win me over. So it's basically possible that Huntley Fitzpatrick wrote it <i>for</i> me, okay? Just so you know. <br /><br />Because it had:<br />• huge emphasis on family...BIG families in fact, which warms my soul because I have big family.<br />• a slow burn romance that started off as a friendship.<br />• all the secondary characters had personalities and lives and <i>brains</i> too, and no one felt like a cardboard cut out.<br />• IT HAD FUNNY MOMENTS<br />• Plenty of food<br />• I think my emotions caught in a knot and I hiccuped with feels, but ya know, that probably <i>wasn't me because I am Vulcan</i>.<br />• Did I mention big families?!?!??!?!?!? <br /><br /><b>What I was most impressed about is how the book did big families RIGHT.</b> It's like a culture, truly! And I loved the <i>details</i>. Even to the point of going to the shop and having comments on "why are you having so many kids" and the prejudice towards mothers who breastfeed. Why not? Why are people terrified by the idea of big families?!?! I'm one of 6. But the Garrett family had EIGHT kids. And they just caught everything soooo weeell. Like having the babies escaping clothes, and mess and calamity, and how the siblings interacted. AWK. &lt;3 <br /><br />(Although to be a complete pain, my only nitpick in that realm is George. I LOVED GEORGE. He is the most adorable endearing 4 year old of the world. But...I have a 4 year old nephew and George was a bit out-of-this-world in terms of facts and cognitive ability and maturity. But hey. Not all 4 year olds are the same. So I'm not going to say kids like George don't exist. THEY DO. [They're also sometimes Autistic but...hm.] I think George was getting all his facts and things from TV, but still. He's only 4. He seemed too mature. Although I did so so love his character.)<br /><br /><b>The story is about Samantha, who lives (OBVIOUSLY!!) next door to the Garrett's.</b> She kind of has this thing about "watching" them. Which could be creepy!? But I related to that. (Maybe I am creepy?) Fascinatingly big families with all their dynamics and life <i>are</i> super captivating to watch. <b>As a character though, I didn't really love Sam.</b> She was quite, calm, collected, rich, perfect...la la la . I don't think she was badly written. I just <b>felt like she had little to no life ambitions.</b> Which I found sad? It's like the quiet characters almost NEVER have life ambitions until they get a boyfriend and wild friends and all that. But *ahem* maybe I'm just being nitpicky here. I didn't hate Sam or anything! I loved her humour and I loved that she was never a snob. And I lvoed that she so easily slotted into babysitting for the Garretts and how she never judged their life choices. OMG.<br /><br /><b>And of COURSE I liked Jase.</b> Although I kept thinking of <i>Jace</i> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/256683.City_of_Bones__The_Mortal_Instruments___1_" title="City of Bones (The Mortal Instruments, #1) by Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">City of Bones</a> because that's the only time I've seen that name. (Although Jase is short for Jason.) He fixed things. *sniffs* He took care of babies. *sniiiiiiffs* He was sweet and yet tough and loved cars and was kind of badass at the same time as being just an adorable golden hearted marshmallow. *sniiiiiiiiiiiiiffs* LEAST TO SAY I SHIPPED IT.<br /><br />And a quickie glance at some of the other secondary characters:<br /><b>• Sam's mum:</b> Yeah she was AWFUL. I'm sure she had OCD with all that obsessive vacuuming too, by the way. But she was definitely being manipulated and she didn't listen to her daughters and AT THE END SHE'S RATHER DESPICABLE. Ugh. A very narrow-minded character. Me no likee.<br /><b>• Tracy (Sam's older sister):</b> Tbh, why was she even in the book? Because she mostly <i>wasn't</i>. <br /><b>• Clay</b>: This is the evil <i>much</i> younger boyfriend of Sam's mum and AGH I HATE HIM SO MUCH HE WAS MANIPULATIVE. By covered it by being smooth and charming. Politics ugh. <br /><b>• Nan:</b> Despite being named after Peter Pan's dog, she was, in fact, not loyal or nice. I didn't like Nan very much because she seemed a bit acidicly jealous towards Sam's life...and then at the end...no Nan. You should've stayed the dog in a children's story.<br /><b>• Tim:</b> Oh Tim, Tim, Tim. At first I hated him. He obviously has some mental health issues and addictions and he was always stoned and drunk. But I don't think having a crappy life EVER excuses you from being a jerk, okay?! OKAY. But then...Tim grew on me. And by the end, even with his failings, at least he was <i>trying</i>, and he was funny. And I just found myself rooting for him to have a better life.<br /><br /><b>Oh and the plot takes you on a WHIRLWIND of emotions!</b> The writing was quite detailed, so I actually didn't whip through the book very fast. But I felt like I was soaking it all in and I really felt INSIDE the story. I could see it all!! And the ending. Woooow wowo wowoowow. I was flipping pages frantically and WAILING. Because it has a huge moral dilemma and it's just all a bit gut-wrenching. And I also appreciated that there weren't any wild drunk parties in this book. LIKE, NONE. I really die a bit at all the contemporaries that have a million parties. Least to say I'm NOT a party animal. So I always kind of zone out. But this had work and family chaos and tragedy and politics and more work (because these teens are earning money and being responsible) and YEAH. I loved that!<br /><br />I ship it. I love it. Big families. Melted ice cream. SERIOUSLY I THINK THIS BOOK IS EVERYTHING. I had me totally caught up. AHHHHHHH. <b>It's basically a 4.5 star rating.</b> And the only reason it doesn't get to the top is it's very LONG and I felt a lot of the time...it was dragging a bit in the middle? Most of the time I was okay with that...but YEAH. Also I really don't understand American politics. I JUST DON'T. So whenever it fell into that jargon I withered like a petunia in the desert. <br /><br /><b>But basically I loved this book.</b> And as a mostly-non-contemporary-reader...THAT IS A BIG DEAL. I wish there were more books with enormous families and all the chaos and love that goes with it. Because it's beautiful and it's challenging and BIG FAMILIES FTW I SAY. (Also entirely shippable romances and cute boys and fabulous witty banter also is awesome. That too.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11061648406609681621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2851329062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2851329062" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2851329062?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142426043" href="/book/show/16101144-my-life-next-door">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2851329062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9825468069536867974">its that time of year again - where i dive into the sweet, summery goodness of YA contemporary perfection! and this would have been the perfect book to kick the season off, had it not done the biggest 180 twisty-turn in the history of surprises. <br/><br/>im not sure if it counts as a spoiler, so i wont mention what happens, but things get very heavy and very dramatic towards the end. i appreciate HF attempting to make this novel deeper than what the genre usually sees but, for me, it doesnt work in this </span>
  <span id="freeText9825468069536867974" style="display:none">its that time of year again - where i dive into the sweet, summery goodness of YA contemporary perfection! and this would have been the perfect book to kick the season off, had it not done the biggest 180 twisty-turn in the history of surprises. <br /><br />im not sure if it counts as a spoiler, so i wont mention what happens, but things get very heavy and very dramatic towards the end. i appreciate HF attempting to make this novel deeper than what the genre usually sees but, for me, it doesnt work in this storys favour. it feels out of place and the complete shock of it didnt allow me to really process it emotionally. i also dont think its wrapped it up well - there are a lot of loose ends and no definite conclusion to many of the problems. i dunno. <br /><br />the first 70% of this is a charmingly fun 4 star read that had me grinning like a fool. but then the entire mood of the book changes and i wasnt quite ready for that. kind of a shame it didnt have a positive impact. :/<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9825468069536867974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_254840395" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254840395" />
    <a title="Glass" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4808910-glass"><img alt="Glass" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583244629p2/4808910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254840395?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glass" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glass" href="/user/show/4808910-glass">Glass</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808910-glass?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254840395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12446693288922487863">This book was worth waiting for. I've read it in two days despite the fact that I was head over heels in all that boring end-of-the-school-year paperwork that us, teachers, are so fond of.<br/><br/> First, I can not believe that this is Huntley Fitzpatrick's debut novel. I've read so many bad books lately and those autors didn't have the excuse of first attempt in their writing carieers. My Life Next Door reminded me a lot of Sarah Dessen novels - by the concept and the writing style. And I love Sarah Des</span>
  <span id="freeText12446693288922487863" style="display:none">This book was worth waiting for. I've read it in two days despite the fact that I was head over heels in all that boring end-of-the-school-year paperwork that us, teachers, are so fond of.<br /><br /> First, I can not believe that this is Huntley Fitzpatrick's debut novel. I've read so many bad books lately and those autors didn't have the excuse of first attempt in their writing carieers. My Life Next Door reminded me a lot of Sarah Dessen novels - by the concept and the writing style. And I love Sarah Dessen.<br /><br /> My Life Next Door is great example of what does it mean to create believable characters - we are introduced with everyone gradually and getting the informations about each characters trought their actions. There isn't author's eulogy about them on five pages or constant describing of every single chlothing choice. (Dear autors, you can describe, but make sure it actally has a point and that it's relevant for the story - like clue in mystery novel. On the other hand, three pages descriptions of what your main heroine is wearing on her first day in school just for the sake of describing is not a good move.)<br /><br /> What I liked the most? The way relationship between Samantha and Jase developed. There's such a positive message for all the young girls - if I had a teenage daughter, I would make her read this book. But it's not just another story about girl who falls for the boy - read it and you'll see.<br /><br /> For the end I can say only one thing - I can't wait for Huntley Fitzpatrick's next novel.<br /><br />P.S. September 8th 2013.<br />I think that I'll re-read this book soon. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12446693288922487863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_352007864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/352007864" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/352007864?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=debut-author-2012">debut-author-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer352007864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17727086159908770331">Rating: 2.5 Stars<br/><br/>Everything about <i> My Life Next Door </i> screams “summer chick-flick”! From its flirty cover, to its sappy title, to its shockingly bright synopsis, you’d think you couldn’t go wrong with this book. I was expected a Sarah Dessen type novel and what I got instead is something I can only relate to authors who I happen to loathe like Stephanie Meyer or Becca Fitzpatrick, even though they’re not contemporary authors. I think what pains me the most is that I <i> really </i> liked the first half</span>
  <span id="freeText17727086159908770331" style="display:none">Rating: 2.5 Stars<br /><br />Everything about <i> My Life Next Door </i> screams “summer chick-flick”! From its flirty cover, to its sappy title, to its shockingly bright synopsis, you’d think you couldn’t go wrong with this book. I was expected a Sarah Dessen type novel and what I got instead is something I can only relate to authors who I happen to loathe like Stephanie Meyer or Becca Fitzpatrick, even though they’re not contemporary authors. I think what pains me the most is that I <i> really </i> liked the first half of this novel. It was slow, it was a little <i> too </i> happy, but it was nice. It had potential. Ultimately though, it just didn’t live up. <br /><br />Samantha Reed seems to have everything – the perfect grade point average, a beautiful home, a rich and successful mother, a perfect figure, and gorgeous genes. Yet, what no one else seems to see is that her mother is hardly a mother – she vacuums obsessively and has been aloof, strict, and apart ever since Sam’s father abandoned their family before she was even born. Thus, Sam cannot help but gaze wistfully at her neighbors, the Garretts, who have eight children, seem to be broke, and yet have all the happiness in the world. When Jase, the third eldest Garrett child, introduces himself to Samantha, her dream of becoming part of their life comes true. Samantha couldn’t be happier – until that is, her senator mother makes a grave mistake that could destroy her newfound happiness and love. <br /><br />I’m not going to lie – I was quite impressed by this story at first. Samantha was an interesting protagonist, one who was suffering underneath her perfect disguise, yet she never let that get in the way of her interactions with others. She constantly tried to be the perfect daughter, the perfect neighbor, the perfect best friend, the perfect girlfriend, and I think that is something everyone can relate to. Yet, Samantha paled in comparison to the Garretts. In some ways, this novel reminded me of Cheaper by the Dozen – two loving parents with a large family of children do their best to make it work. Furthermore, these kids, despite their vastly different personalities, all love one another and seem to mesh perfectly as siblings. Seeing Samantha fit into this equation was nothing short of entertaining and only increased my respect for her. <br /><br />In addition to the Garretts though, another family that played a huge part in this novel was Sam’s best friend Nan and her brother Tim. Sam has grown up with these two since childhood and I loved how realistically their relationships were portrayed – well, in the first half of the novel. Usually, authors never give too much emphasis to the best friend, but Nan was given a lot of importance in this story, which I liked – especially because a friend’s problems, their life, and their struggles impact your life as well. Furthermore, Tim, Nan’s older brother, undergoes immense growth and change throughout this novel as well as being one hell of an intelligent, sassy, and funny guy – all qualities which instantaneously made him my favorite character. Although I loved Jase, the main love interest, Tim was simply so much <i> more. </i> Jase is kind, polite, and perfect to the point where he has no flaws. He is an attentive boyfriend, a doting son, an inspirting brother, and an adoring child in general. Sam’s relationship with Jase was cute, fun, and likeable. They had their awkward moments, their gradual growth, and their eventual path to love. I liked all of these things, but somewhere after the half-way point of this book, everything began to go downhill. <br /><br />First and foremost, one of the main issues that can be seen even from the beginning of the novel is the fact that Sam’s mother hates Jase’s family. She thinks they’re too big and she despises that since her own unreliable husband came from a family just like theirs. So of course, when Sam becomes involved with Jase her mother doesn’t know about it and surprisingly enough, neither does Sam’s best friend. Logically speaking, this should have been a big problem in the story. Jase <i> should </i> have been very upset by this, he <i> should </i> have seriously questioned Sam’s feelings for him, but he didn’t, because you know, Jase is just <i> such </i> a sweet and forgiving guy. Is this realistic? No, not even close. Strike #1 <br /><br />Although Problem #1 bothered me, I was able to let it go and trudge onwards with the story to Problem #2. This is a friendship problem with Nan – one which, in my opinion, was original, different, and really interesting. I wanted to see how this played out! I was curious, I was excited – uniqueness in YA Contemporary Fiction? It was unheard of! Yet, what winds up happening in this situation is that Nan refuses to speak to Sam and even after Sam <i> finally </i> gets the backbone and guts to force Nan to speak to her, they have a short conversation and end their friendship of twelve years <i> just like that. </i> I don’t know about you, but I wouldn’t walk away from my best friend of twelve years that easily. I let it go though, I kept thinking it would come up later, that it would be resolved <i> eventually. </i> Spoiler Alert: That eventual closure we’re waiting for? It doesn’t happen. Sam doesn’t even get to say her perspective of the issue in fact! She just listens to Nan, nods, walks away, and Nan is never mentioned ever again. Irritating? Yes. Unrealistic? Yes. Strike #2? Yes.<br /><br />If you haven’t already figured out so far, Samantha has some serious issues – not only in her life, but with her personality as well. Most importantly, she has no backbone. A Gryffindor she most certainly is not. She lacks the courage to tell her mom about her perfect boyfriend, she lacks the courage to salvage her friendship with Nan, but the last straw comes when she lacks the courage <i> to do what is right. </i> This is a spoiler-free review (for the most part), so all I can really say is that her mother does something bad – really bad – and it affects the Garretts, who are poor and struggling to make ends meet, in a really bad way. Samantha <i> knows </i> that her mother is responsible for this act that is causing the Garretts to suffer, but no one else knows about it, so what should she do? Well, first of all, she should tell her boyfriend. What she <i> does </i> do instead though, is tell herself that what she thinks isn’t true – denial. I’m not heartless, so I can accept denial, but not for eight days (or a week…something like that)! Plus, even <i> after </i> that eight days, when she finally accepts it’s true, she <i> still </i> doesn’t tell Jase! This entire situation plays out in <i> such </i> a ridiculous manner that it is not even funny. Sam’s mother is Senator Reed, running for re-election, so the truth can’t com out because of her campaign, but you know what? I don’t care. Everyone is raised with a moral sense of right from wrong and the decisions Sam and her mother make are wrong, irritating, and disappointing. Of course this situation all solves itself up very nicely, but I hated its entire presence in the novel. Not only does it take up the entire second half of the novel, it <i> ruins </i> it. Strike #3<br /><br />Avid baseball fans (or not-baseball-fans like me) will know that after three strikes, you are <i> out </i> and boy, was this book out – out of my shelf, out of my life, <i> out. </i> What upsets me the most though, is that this book had a <i> lot </i> of potential. It had unique and original ideas, but its execution of them was disappointing and lacking. I think the author’s intention was for this novel to be an expose about how a girl who seems to have everything together really doesn’t. How she makes mistakes, loses friends and her life falls apart. Well, Sam’s life <i> did </i> fall apart, but that was because of stupid mistakes, idiotic decisions, and loss of a brain for eight days. I suppose some may argue that that <i> is </i> life, it <i> is </i> realistic, but if you read this book you’ll know that these situations and the way they were handled were <i> not </i> realistic. Furthermore, Sam’s sister was only in this novel for 2% of it which was a huge mistake. I kept thinking of how things would have been different if Sam’s sister was there and I think it would have been a stronger novel if her relationship with her sister was allowed to develop. <br /><br />Gosh, that brings me to <i> another </i> problem! There was no development of relationships in this novel except between Sam and the Garretts and Tim with…well everyone because he’s just awesome like that. Even by the end of the novel, Sam’s mother felt like the same Crappy Mom of the Decade since she was being a selfish pig. Furthermore, I haven’t even mention Supreme Villain of All Time, Clay. Clay is a douche bag, an idiot, a guy with the wrong priorities and he also happens to be Senator Reed’s boyfriend. *cue gag* I don’t want to talk about him, I hate him, and all you need to know is that he sucks. <br /><br /><i> My Life Next Door </i> is a novel with a lot of potential, a lot of hope, and a lot of disappointment. The first half of this book is sweet, caring, and fun but then it just becomes strike after strike after strike. After reading it, I can’t even say that I liked it. If anything, I feel as if I wasted a huge chunk of my time. Looking back, I don’t even feel that invested in Sam and Jase’s relationship since Jase was so perfect and Sam was so unworthy of him and any problems they had weren’t even dealt with in a realistic and proper manner. *sigh* I’m sorry to say that <i> My Life Next Door </i> goes right back on my shelf of disappointing debuts. Fitzpatrick had some great ideas in this one, but everything just fell flat in the end. Perhaps a more experienced author would have been better suited to write such a complex novel, but Fitzpatrick was simply unable to handle the plethora of scenarios in this one. That being said…I. Am. Out. <br /><br />You can find this review and more on my blog, <a href="http://ivybookbindings.blogspot.com/2012/06/review-my-life-next-door-by-huntley.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Ivy Book Bindings</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17727086159908770331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032303826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10201737941871681454"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444333304i/16485141._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Why, thank you book for all these <i>wonderful</i> platitudes.</b> We need to part ways now though, at 35%, but don't worry, I'll compile here every <i>amazing</i> moment we shared together.<br/><br/>► <b>Remember when Jase and Sam fell in love over a lemonade at 9%?</b> Because I was there to follow their <i>astounding banter</i> and was <i>deeply moved</i> by the <i>slow burn</i> of their feelings.... <br/><br/><blockquote>
<i>"He drains the entire thing in one gulp, then reaches for the other cup. <br/>"That's mine," I say.<br/>"Oh, jeez. Of course. Sorry. I</i> am<i> thirsty."<br/>I extend my</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10201737941871681454" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444333304i/16485141._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Why, thank you book for all these <i>wonderful</i> platitudes.</b> We need to part ways now though, at 35%, but don't worry, I'll compile here every <i>amazing</i> moment we shared together.<br><br>► <b>Remember when Jase and Sam fell in love over a lemonade at 9%?</b> Because I was there to follow their <i>astounding banter</i> and was <i>deeply moved</i> by the <i>slow burn</i> of their feelings.... <br><br><blockquote>
<i>"He drains the entire thing in one gulp, then reaches for the other cup. <br>"That's mine," I say.<br>"Oh, jeez. Of course. Sorry. I</i> am<i> thirsty."<br>I extend my arm with the lemonade. "You can have it. There's always more."<br>He shakes his head. "I would never deprive you."<br><b>I feel my stomach do that weird little flip-flop thing you hear about.</b>"</i>
</blockquote><br>It's not insta-love guys, because it's not the first time they talk. Nope. It's the <i>second</i> time, not to mention that she has stalked him for years. Of course it counts! <br><br>► <b>Remember when Jase kept telling Sam such <i>profound and life changing</i> sentences?</b> I swear the guy must be an hidden philosopher gem or something.<br><br><blockquote>
<i>"No, thank God. I'd die if I got in trouble."<br>Jase looks at me intently, as though what I've said is profound"</i> ← SEE?<br><i><b>"No, you wouldn't, Samantha. You wouldn't die. You'd just be in trouble and then you'd move on."</b></i>
</blockquote><br>MY GOD. Who needs Sartre when Jase is in the house? I might quote him someday. <br><br>► <b>Remember when we met the most oblivious parents of the world?</b> I know teenagers are tricky, but there must be a medal hiding somewhere for Nan and Tim's ones. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I know!" she says. "It's so much worst since he got kicked out of Ellery. He spends <b>all day like this</b> [STONED &amp; DRUNKED <u>AT HOME</u>], and God knows what he does at night. <b>My parents are completely and totally without a clue. Mommy buys all his lies - 'Oh, that's catnip in that bag, Ma. Oh, those pills? Aspirin. That white stuff? Just salt.</b>"</i>
</blockquote><br>... and it's not finished : <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"He's [the Obvious Dad] even got Tim's <b>pot plant in with his own plants, giving it Miracle-Gro</b>. What kind of man was young in the eighties and doesn't recognize marijuana?"</i>
</blockquote><br>Who indeed? Should we warn someone? Put them on TV or something? Huh? (Not that Nan would tell them, of course. I mean, it's only her brother's life for fuck sake. FUCK. FUCK OFF. FUCK. FUCK. ← <b>Tim's favorite words if any.</b><br><br>► <b>Remember when Sam caught her mum's boyfriend (probably) cheating and didn't say a thing?</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"How can I say "Uh - Mom - I think he might be seeing someone else too"?</i>
</blockquote><br>...<br>.........<br>Hmm... Like this? Oh, no? You don't want to? Okay.<br><br>► <b>Remember when Jase <i>thoughtfully</i> listened to Sam's <i>Earth shattering</i> conversations?</b> I'm pretty sure it's one of my fave parts. I mean, come on. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"How did you get so good at everything?" I ask Jase as he wipes his greasy hands on a rag from his tool kit.<br><b>"At everything," he repeats thoughtfully."</b></i>
</blockquote><br>I might <i>combust</i> from butterflies each time he opens his thoughtful mouth - and it keeps getting better and better! <br><br>► <b>Remember when Sam and me agreed on something?</b> Frankly, it just made my day. Truly. Hope to die and all that shit. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Jase's green eyes meet mine, then his lashes lower. "I guess I like things that take time and attention. More worthwhile that way."<br><b>I don't know what it is about this that makes me blush, but something does."</b></i>
</blockquote><br>You and me on this, girl. Wait - NO! I didn't <i>blush</i>! What I mean is that I have no clue about why this (wonderfully profound as always) sentence is blush worthy. NOT A FREAKING CLUE (explanations in comments are welcome). That SOMETHING though.<br><br>► <b>Remember when ... </b><br><br>OH BOY. Can I just forget it? To me <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door" title="My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">My Life Next Door</a> is silly, filled with <u>platitudes</u> and <u>flat dialogues</u>, bland and stereotypical characters I don't give a shit about (including <u>a perfect snowflake</u> and an absent mum), an <u>instalovish romance with no chemistry whatsoever</u> and -</b> Well, I guess that's all. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429295103i/14566469._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4455740454690454619">WHAT IS HAPPENING.<br/><br/>For many years, I have thought that this and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989213506' rel='nofollow noopener'>On the Fence</a> were the same book.   <span id="freeText4455740454690454619" style="display:none">WHAT IS HAPPENING.<br /><br />For many years, I have thought that this and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989213506" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Fence</a> were the same book. Then I reread them back to back, for I am a fool.<br /><br />Now, I somehow liked this book markedly less than On the Fence??<br /><br />Even though On the Fence is by Kasie West, my mortal frenemy???<br /><br />We live in a lawless, senseless world. A realm of chaos and confusion and pain.<br /><br />Anyway. Back to this summery YA contemporary.<br /><br />What I expected from this book: summer, friendship, banter, some light romance, a nice coming of age in the background<br /><br />What I got: Suffering. Drama. Angst. So much angst, in fact, that I would not be surprised to learn that Huntley Fitzpatrick headed up the writer’s room on the television program Degrassi. (Because that show was filled with angst. Get it?)<br /><br />This just felt way too heavy and dramatic in a way that seemed very pointless. Also, I did not care for the characters much at all, so it was a slog to get through it.<br /><br />Now that I’ve used the word “slog,” it’s clearly time to wrap this one up.<br /><br />Bottom line: This was a fairly quick read, and that’s the nicest thing I can say about it.<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />this book was so angsty i could feel my blood pressure slowly.....creeping.....up.........<br /><br />review to come (post-cardiac arrest)<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />for a long time, i thought this and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989213506?type=review#rating_210732374" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Fence</a> were the same book. now i am binge-rereading them back to back, i guess to doom myself to a fate of getting them mixed up forever</span>

<div id="review_298203397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298203397" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298203397?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=adorable-favourites">adorable-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=best-of-2012">best-of-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=boys-i-wish-were-real">boys-i-wish-were-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=prose-perfect">prose-perfect</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298203397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12168404548552684147"><b>Rating:</b> 4.95 brilliant, beautiful, breathtaking stars out of 5!<br/><br/><u>FACT #1:</u> I'm not a contemporary girl. I love paranormal books way more than my realistic ones; worlds that don't really exist enthrall me way more than real ones do. Because those supernatural books are usually more badass, intense, and fun than everyday romances.<br/><br/><u>FACT #2:</u> <b>My Life Next Door</b> totally voids the first fact!!<br/><br/>Where can I even start with how much I loved this book? How much it took me surprise, grabbed my heart, and wouldn't</span>
  <span id="freeText12168404548552684147" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> 4.95 brilliant, beautiful, breathtaking stars out of 5!<br /><br /><u>FACT #1:</u> I'm not a contemporary girl. I love paranormal books way more than my realistic ones; worlds that don't really exist enthrall me way more than real ones do. Because those supernatural books are usually more badass, intense, and fun than everyday romances.<br /><br /><u>FACT #2:</u> <b>My Life Next Door</b> totally voids the first fact!!<br /><br />Where can I even start with how much I loved this book? How much it took me surprise, grabbed my heart, and wouldn't let go? This is NOTHING like your average contemporary read! It's still sweet and romantic and funny and brilliant. But I thought I had a good guess to what the huge plot twist would be, and boy was I wrong! I didn't expect it <i>at all</i>, which doesn't happen with me and contemporaries very often.<br /><br />And the cast — I loved <i>every single character</i>! They were all so perfectly, brilliantly, wonderfully written. There's Sam, who I ached for, because she grows up with the pressure to be perfect from a mother who doesn't know the definition of fun. Then there's Jase, and God, I loved him so much! ♥ He wears a leather jacket, drives a motorcycle, and is the boy next door... but he is undoubtedly the SWEETEST book boy I've ever met. <i>Ever</i>. I'm not even kidding!<br /><br />(I already have our wedding colours picked out. He's seriously WONDERFUL!)<br /><br />But I can't forget mentioning the entire Garrett family! Made up of eight totally individual children and two adoring parents, the Garretts are my dream family. Loud, fun, hilarious, affectionate. Obviously Jase is my favourite, but George — Jase's adorable 4-year-old brother who watches too much Discovery Channel for his own good — was a close favourite! :')<br /><br />The humor! The wit! The complexity! This book was funny like I didn't expect, and heartwarming in ways I never imagined. The only reason (and I mean ONLY) that this book gets a 4.95 instead of a full 5 stars is because I felt like the ending didn't wrap up enough.<br /><br />With one of the funnest contemporary casts of all time, an extremely sweet and beautiful romance, and a twist that will be a surprise, <b>My Life Next Door</b> is undoubtedly one of the best contemporaries of all time — and one of my all-time favourites as well!<br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> Why are you even thinking about this question?? I bought this book on a whim and it became a favourite. Start saving up your change because this is WAY worth the buy — I'm actually a little tempted to buy two copies!<br /><br />-Mimi<br /><br /><b>P.S.</b> My older sister read this book in two days... and she hasn't read another book in six months! Now try and TELL ME that the amazingness of this book is just in my head! x) <br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.ca/2012/07/review-my-life-next-door.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12168404548552684147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13971937399462244031"><span>[image error]</span> <br/><br/>What an enjoyable young adult story! Samantha is the daughter of the Connecticut’s Senator and has lived next door the the large Garrett family for many years. She watches them but never engages until the summer before her senior year when she meets Jase Garrett and his seven siblings. Her mother is a real piece of work and not only looks down on the Garrett family but gets caught up with her new campaign guy Clay and lacks a lot of the important mom skills. The author throws in a </span>
  <span id="freeText13971937399462244031" style="display:none"><span>[image error]</span> <br><br>What an enjoyable young adult story! Samantha is the daughter of the Connecticut’s Senator and has lived next door the the large Garrett family for many years. She watches them but never engages until the summer before her senior year when she meets Jase Garrett and his seven siblings. Her mother is a real piece of work and not only looks down on the Garrett family but gets caught up with her new campaign guy Clay and lacks a lot of the important mom skills. The author throws in a great cast of charters, adorable younger Garrett kids and a pure love story.<br><br><b>
  <i>“You have to kiss me," I find myself saying.<br>"Yeah." He leans closer. "I do.” </i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491796595ra/22447688.gif" width="390" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Samantha is faced with doing the right thing when she realizes that her mother has affected the Garrett family in which she has become a pseudo member. Jase and Samantha’s relationship was adorable, snarky, and well done and I’m excited to find another great author. The story wasn’t too young for my tastes but just the right amount of first love, summer fun, and villain drama.<br><br><b>
  <i>”What Jase and I have is real and alive. It has nothing to do with how things look from far away and everything to do with the how they are up close.”</i>

<span id="freeTextContainer16534088522266060254"><b>*3.5 Stars*</b><br/><br/>A fun and refreshing, sweet summer read! The writing was fluid and wonderfully captured the essence of being a teen in a very realistic manner. <br/><br/>While the story didn't necessarily blow me away, it certainly held my interest and warmed my heart. <br/><br/><b>Samantha </b> is a young girl who, at first glance, appears to have it all. She's beautiful, wealthy, and has a determined mother in politics who keeps up a perfect appearance for their well-respected family. <br/><br/>But Samantha isn't happy. <br/><br/>Because her mo</span>
  <span id="freeText16534088522266060254" style="display:none"><b>*3.5 Stars*</b><br><br>A fun and refreshing, sweet summer read! The writing was fluid and wonderfully captured the essence of being a teen in a very realistic manner. <br><br>While the story didn't necessarily blow me away, it certainly held my interest and warmed my heart. <br><br><b>Samantha </b> is a young girl who, at first glance, appears to have it all. She's beautiful, wealthy, and has a determined mother in politics who keeps up a perfect appearance for their well-respected family. <br><br>But Samantha isn't happy. <br><br>Because her motivated-mommy is cold, selfish, and emotionally distant; placing more care in her work-life than in their home.<br><br>From the porch outside her bedroom window, Samantha longingly watches the large and lively family living next door. <br><br>The Garrett's are everything Samantha's mother is not: unorganized, noisy, messy, and genuinely unconcerned with the opinions of others. <br><br>But they are also a happy, loving family, and Samantha cannot help becoming drawn to their unique lifestyle. For Samantha, watching them is like dreaming--until one day <b>Jase</b> climbs up to her window, and the Garrett's finally materialize. <br><br>This story's pace is slow and steady. Jase and Sam build an instant friendship that leads slowly to young love. <br><br>However, all is not perfect, and Jase and Sam eventually find themselves facing a very real crisis. One that could ultimately tear them apart. <br><br>I'm aware that a certain degree of tension must be added in a story, but I'm not sure I loved the specifics of this one. It's not that the turn it took wasn't believable, but I felt my heart just wasn't all-in. <br><br>I did see some readers mention that the ending was a bit disappointing. While I typically prefer a more abrupt, less detailed ending, I must agree with the general opinion in this case. The story didn't feel like it actually ended -- it felt as if it just fell off. Like it was dropped. I wanted to pick it back up ... but, alas, there was no more. <br><br>All things considered, I did enjoy the story and would certainly recommend to those in search of a charming, YA summer read.<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪	 Genre/Category:</b> Romance/YA<br><b>▪	 Steam Caliber:</b> Mild.<br><b>▪ Romance:</b> Sweet. Young love. <br><b>▪	 Characters:</b> Lonely heroine. Sweet, lively hero.<br><b>▪	 Plot:</b> Two young teens from opposite backgrounds find love. <br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Fluid.<br><b>▪ POV:</b> 1st Person: Heroine<br><b>▪	 Cliffhanger:</b> None. Standalone.<br><b>▪ HEA? </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><a href="http://prettywordsbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_352370574" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/352370574" />
    <a title="Karla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3024056-karla"><img alt="Karla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324910771p2/3024056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/352370574?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/3024056-karla">Karla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15713279-my-life-next-door">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Karla by: </span>
      Marie Francis
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=angst-filled">angst-filled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=spunky-heroine">spunky-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=sweet-boy">sweet-boy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=wonderful-secondary-characters">wonderful-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=youthful-angst">youthful-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=intense">intense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=terrific-dialogue">terrific-dialogue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=sweet-romance">sweet-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer352370574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10033930813647900636"><b>4 1/2 Stars!!</b> This was a 5 plus star read for me…until the end, because there really wasn’t one, or at least not one that satisfied me. I only detracted a half a star, because the rest of the book was amazing. I enjoyed the comparisons and stereotypes of two completely different families.<br/><br/>Samantha is a sweet, determined young woman who is showcased, yet sheltered by her mother. After many years of observing the family next door, she finally meets Jase, the third oldest in the Garrett clan. He app</span>
  <span id="freeText10033930813647900636" style="display:none"><b>4 1/2 Stars!!</b> This was a 5 plus star read for me…until the end, because there really wasn’t one, or at least not one that satisfied me. I only detracted a half a star, because the rest of the book was amazing. I enjoyed the comparisons and stereotypes of two completely different families.<br><br>Samantha is a sweet, determined young woman who is showcased, yet sheltered by her mother. After many years of observing the family next door, she finally meets Jase, the third oldest in the Garrett clan. He approaches her as she’s sitting on the roof ledge by her window, observing the life going on next door, so different from the one she lives. This loving, loud, energetic family embraces and welcomes her into the fold, and Sam thrives on it. She falls in love with them and Jase. He is the type of boy parents dream that their daughter will bring home, but Samantha’s mother can’t see past the image of the large family with the unkempt yard and their somewhat chaotic life. She can’t see how good and loving these people are because her mind is clouded by the stereotype; messy yard, large brood equates to trailer trash! <b>WRONG, WRONG, WRONG!!</b> Fortunately Sam is a better person than her mother could ever dream to be, and sees the Garrett's for what they really are; a messy yard, large brood, chaotic life and an overabundance of <b>LOVE</b> for each other and living!<br><br>It is basically a clean romance; however Jase and Sam do explore their sexuality. The author was very responsible by making them responsible. Jase and Sam take their time with this life-changing event, and the author injected some humor to lighten the mood. The condom conversation was priceless. <br><br>A heartrending event occurs in the book that affects both families and I don’t really want to say too much, other than I felt like someone punched me in the stomach. It was so painful to read about! Here’s where I had a problem, not with the tragic event, but with the ending. I’m became enthralled by these two families and the author captivated me with the story. The tragedy is addressed, but the outcome isn’t…not enough to satisfy this reader. I have no doubt that others will feel the same. I felt cheated and anxious after turning the last page. There was also a matter that arose between Sam and her best friend Nan that was not resolved. A chapter or two more and it would have changed my entire view on the book. * heavy sigh*!<br><br>That being said,<b> for a debut book it is terrific</b>, and the author has real talent. Jase’s younger brother George is one of the most memorable characters I ever had the pleasure to read about, and I adored him, as I did the entire Garrett brood. Tim, Nan’s brother is my hero. He went from loser to savior; I would love to read a book about him!<br><br>Even though I was dissatisfied with the ending myself, I would still recommend this book. BUT if you are someone who needs the ending to wrap up nicely, beware! Jase and Sam get their HEA, but so many questions remain unanswered. <br><br><b>"Sun-streaked, wavy chestnut hair and even white teeth, Jase Garrett has green eyes, and one of those quirky mouths that look like they are always about to smile."</b><br><a href="http://s1130.photobucket.com/albums/m524/kparks823/?action=view&amp;current=evangeiselman-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381414i/738716.jpg" alt="evangeiselman" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10033930813647900636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
