<div id="review_295974524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/295974524" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/295974524?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295974524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14887192599707625986">One of my favourite boys in YA contemporary fiction is Étienne St. Clair from <em>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___1_' title='Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anna and the French Kiss</a>
</em> and Jase Garrett from <em>My Life Next Door</em> is now up there with him!<br/><br/>Seventeen-year-old Samantha Reed lives a quiet, stable life compared to her neighbours. The Garretts are loud and chaotic and everything Samantha's senator mother tries to avoid, so Samantha knows her mother would not be happy that she has fallen in love with Jase. Jase's parents and their seven other children – Joel, Alice, A</span>
  <span id="freeText14887192599707625986" style="display:none">One of my favourite boys in YA contemporary fiction is Étienne St. Clair from <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6936382.Anna_and_the_French_Kiss__Anna_and_the_French_Kiss___1_" title="Anna and the French Kiss (Anna and the French Kiss, #1) by Stephanie Perkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna and the French Kiss</a>
</em> and Jase Garrett from <em>My Life Next Door</em> is now up there with him!<br /><br />Seventeen-year-old Samantha Reed lives a quiet, stable life compared to her neighbours. The Garretts are loud and chaotic and everything Samantha's senator mother tries to avoid, so Samantha knows her mother would not be happy that she has fallen in love with Jase. Jase's parents and their seven other children – Joel, Alice, Andy (Andrea), Duff, Harry, George and Patsy – welcome Samantha into their home. She joins them for meals, helps Andy decide what to wear on her first date and babysits George and Patsy. But Samantha's mother is completely unaware of her daughter's secret life next door, too focused on her own political campaign – until tragedy strikes. Samantha must first convince herself to do what's right.<br /><br /><em>My Life Next Door </em>is everything I want from a YA contemporary novel: a close-knit American town setting; a realistic and believable romance; a supportive and loving family (especially toddler George!); intense friendships; and quite a bit of drama. I'm part of a small family and struggle to imagine what it must be like to be one of eight children, but I loved reading about the Garretts, and watching Samantha figure out how to navigate their world. Aside from the wonderful romance between Jase and Samantha – which develops slowly and naturally, and is a lot fun to read – friendship is also important to the story, particularly how the two teenagers deal with twins Tim and Nan, both struggling in their own ways.<br /><br /><em>My Life Next Door</em> was the perfect summer romance story – until it took a more unexpected, serious turn. We get to see whether Samantha and Jase's relationship can withstand the pressure as their lives come crashing down, affecting not only their own relationship, but the strong bonds between family and friends, too.<br /><br />I adored <em>My Life Next Door</em>. It absolutely should not have taken me three years to pick it up. Hopefully it won't take me another three to read the companion novel, <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18392495.The_Boy_Most_Likely_To" title="The Boy Most Likely To by Huntley Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">The Boy Most Likely To</a>
</em>.<br /><br /><br /><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="14887192599707625986" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11145701502217586341"><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432081i/867706.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My Life Next Door tells us the story of Samantha, a girl who practically has spent her 17 years <b>watching The Garrets. All the time </b><br/><br/>The Garrets are her neighbors next door and Sam’s mother hates them because they remind her of her ex- in laws. They are a huge family, very noisy and carefree, they are happy. And even though Sam’s mom told her to never ever have contact with them she can’t help but stare at them all the time.<br/><br/>And one night while she’s spying them, Jase comes to “rescue her”.<br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>”Hey,</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText11145701502217586341" style="display:none"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432081i/867706.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My Life Next Door tells us the story of Samantha, a girl who practically has spent her 17 years <b>watching The Garrets. All the time </b><br><br>The Garrets are her neighbors next door and Sam’s mother hates them because they remind her of her ex- in laws. They are a huge family, very noisy and carefree, they are happy. And even though Sam’s mom told her to never ever have contact with them she can’t help but stare at them all the time.<br><br>And one night while she’s spying them, Jase comes to “rescue her”.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>”Hey, need rescuing?” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432081i/867707.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>From that moment, they can’t stay apart. They always have an excuse to see each other and that’s how Samantha is introduced to that crazy family called The Garrets. I cannot name them all but let me say George was my favourite.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Is Jase already gonna marry you?”<br><br>I start coughing again. “Uh, No. No, George. I’m only seventeen.” As if that’s the only reason we’re not engaged.<br><br>“I’m this many.” George holds up four, slightly grubby fingers. “But Jase is seventeen and a half. You could. Then you could live in here with him. And have a big family.”<br><br>Jase strides back into the room, of course, midway through this proposition. “George. Beat it. Discovery Channel is on.”<br><br>George backs out of the room but not before saying, “His bed’s really comfortable. And he never pees in it.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br>So they start a beautiful friendship that ends up involving love feelings but they don’t want to take things quick so they remain friends... for a while.<br><br>Sam’s best friend Nan also plays an important role in this story <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ FUCKING BITCH!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and her brother Tim. He was one of my fave characters and I would have love to see him and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Alice  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> together. Tim doesn’t have an easy life but he was a good example for a lot of young guys that are totally lost and don’t know what to do with their lifes.<br><br>Sam’s mom was… AGH! I don’t even have words, not to mention her boyfriend and all that happened <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ with the accident  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>But I guess Jase made it up for me big time because he was PERFECT! I have ZERO complains about him.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>”I guess I like things that take time and attention. More worthwhile that way” </blockquote>
</b><br><br>And yeah… I have a tiny complain. Where the hell is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the end??? Seriously!!! I am missing it. I know I have an imagination and blah blah blah but come on!!!<br><br>And that resolution about the accident? Nope, I didn’t like that  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>All in all, this was a very well written sweet summer story that will take you back to your younger years. A story that will make you dream and believe that everything is possible in this world if you find your Jase.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380432081i/867708.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Thanks Sandra for telling me about this book and for our BR.<br></i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11145701502217586341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer440933324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8107695815601472811"> <b>2.5 I'M-HAVING-AN-ANGER-ATTACK-OVER-HERE STARS<br/><br/>Thank you dear Rosalinda for BR with me <3 </b><br/><br/>There were quite a few characters i really wanted to stab in the eye and push off a cliff. Let's make a list.<br/><br/>1. Samantha (but only towards the end).<br/>2. Gracie (Samantha's mother)<br/>3. Clay (Samantha's mum boyfriend).<br/>4. Nan (Samantha's BFF). <br/><br/><a href='http://postimage.org/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395362ra/761474.gif' alt='ways to1' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a target='_blank' href='http://postimage.org/app.php' rel='nofollow noopener'></a><br/><br/><br/><br/>But for my sake i'm going to keep this review short and sweet. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>One thing my mother never knew, and would dissaprove of most of all, was that i watched the Garretts. A</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8107695815601472811" style="display:none"> <b>2.5 I'M-HAVING-AN-ANGER-ATTACK-OVER-HERE STARS<br><br>Thank you dear Rosalinda for BR with me &lt;3 </b><br><br>There were quite a few characters i really wanted to stab in the eye and push off a cliff. Let's make a list.<br><br>1. Samantha (but only towards the end).<br>2. Gracie (Samantha's mother)<br>3. Clay (Samantha's mum boyfriend).<br>4. Nan (Samantha's BFF). <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395362ra/761474.gif" alt="ways to1" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>But for my sake i'm going to keep this review short and sweet. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>One thing my mother never knew, and would dissaprove of most of all, was that i watched the Garretts. All the time.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395362i/761475._SY540_.jpg" alt="eceae039 0007 4026 b13c 70f0f59adb17 zpsec12dfb4" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>17 year old Samantha Reeds spent half her life watching the Garrets next door. They were everything she and her family were not - loud, happy, messy, loving. She wished she would be one of them.<br><br>Until one summer day Jase Garrett climbs up next to her on the roof and changes everything.<br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395362i/761476.jpg" alt="360f8d59 f191 492d 829c d7ec792d209b zps987afafd" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>As the two fall fiercely for each other, stumbling through awkwardness and awesomeness of first love, something unthinkable happens and Samantha's world starts crumbling. She's suddenly faced with an impossible decision. <br><br><b>Which perfect family will save her? Or is it time she saved herself?</b><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380395362i/761477.jpg" alt="depression quotes" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><b>Someone should have warned me that people who have anger issues shouldn't read this book.</b> Someone damn right should have said something! The last couple of pages i have been wanting to <b>shred the whole book to pieces</b>. Why? Naturally because of the MC Samantha. <br><br><b>Samantha</b><br>I liked her in the beginning but at the end she became so freaking annoying i had to stop reading, take deep breaths and calm damn before i would set the book on fire (and trust me, i've done it once before).<br>I wished she would <b>stand up for herself</b> and not let her stupid mother live her life for her. And she shouldn't have just taken the way her mum's boyfriend treats her. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When he blackmailed her and she just took it i was so angry at her! She should kick his balls and tell him to fuck off.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Teen MC really get me angry when they don't have a little attitude and listen to everything their parents say like some dogs. Sam was a very boring character, she was too good, and didn't do anything exciting like i think every girl her age should do. Have a little adventure!<br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395362ra/761478.gif" alt="tumblr mj7k6l Ey2u1rfzcyho2 250" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br><b>
  <u>What i liked?</u>
</b><br>- The romance between Jace and Sam (really sweet).<br>- The Garretts family (Joel should get his own book, he's my fav).<br>- That Sam was still working even though she didn't need to<br>- Writing Style<br><br><b>
  <u>What i didn't like?</u>
</b><br>- How much family drama there was ( i got enough of my own, thank you very much).<br>- Some of the characters i mentioned before<br>- How slow the book was (in my opinion).<br>- That Samantha didn't fight back<br>- The ending (even though it was HEA i felt like some things were left unsolved).<br>- And that Samantha kept quite about the whole 'accident' instead of saying something like she should have. <br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395362ra/761479.gif" alt="tumblr ltcjyo5y IO1qf4ea2o1 500" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/app.php" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
</a><br><br><br><br><b>Overall, <i>My Life Next Door</i> was...</b><br><br><a href="http://postimage.org/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380395362ra/761480.gif" alt="original" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" href="http://postimage.org/" rel="nofollow noopener"></a><br><br><br><br>Not an amazing read that i couldn't wait to get back to for sure. But it was an alright, cute, summer read. Jase was a real sweetheart that i loved and his whole family was awesome! <br><br>Don't let my review stop you from reading this, you will most likely enjoy it more than i did :)<br><br><br><br><br><br><b>
  <u></u>
</b><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b></b>

<div id="review_1881522454" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881522454" />
    <a title="Jiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana"><img alt="Jiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540380229p2/10502567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1881522454?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101575222" href="/book/show/16692543-my-life-next-door">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1881522454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6845122725910053376"><blockquote>
  <i>“Who are these people, and why do they think their own opinions are the only right ones?”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>My Life Next Door is one of those super adorable contemporary novels you'd read if you want to pass the time. I really liked it yet I had a few issues with it. The plot has several themes, some of which are family, belonging, doing what's right... The plot was also heavily centered around politics, which wasn't interesting for me. I've never cared about politics. I don't understand it and it never intere</span>
  <span id="freeText6845122725910053376" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Who are these people, and why do they think their own opinions are the only right ones?”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />My Life Next Door is one of those super adorable contemporary novels you'd read if you want to pass the time. I really liked it yet I had a few issues with it. The plot has several themes, some of which are family, belonging, doing what's right... The plot was also heavily centered around politics, which wasn't interesting for me. I've never cared about politics. I don't understand it and it never interests me. In this book, I was quickly distracted during scenes about politics.<br /><br />Another issue was the plot. <b>There was no plot</b>. The plot kinda started around the 75-80% mark, if I'm not mistaken. Before that, it was just Samantha's daily life and her growing relationship with Jase and his family. Samantha talks about her job, her mother, her best friend, her best friend's brother and just everyday events. I didn't like that. It made the book <i>too</i> long.<br /><br />Now, what did save the book was the Garretts. <b>WHAT A WONDERFUL FAMILY.</b> I have so much love for them! They're all so tight and they all love each and they're all so precious! My favorite (other than Jase of course) is the little cutie, George, Jase's 4 year old brother). Oh my God, he's beyond adorable! <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Is Jase already gonna marry you?”<br /><br />I start coughing again. “Uh, No. No, George. I’m only seventeen.” As if that’s the only reason we’re not engaged.<br /><br />“I’m this many.” George holds up four, slightly grubby fingers. “But Jase is seventeen and a half. You could. Then you could live in here with him. And have a big family.”<br /><br />Jase strides back into the room, of course, midway through this proposition. “George. Beat it. Discovery Channel is on.”<br /><br />George backs out of the room but not before saying, “His bed’s really comfortable. And he never pees in it.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>TELL ME HE ISN'T THE MOST PRECIOUS THING IN THE ENTIRE WORLD???</b><br /><br />Now, Jase Garrett, our male MC. He's just so lovely! He's great. He's sweet and he's so <i>good</i>. We need more good guys in books. Jase is a great brother, a great son, and a wonderful boyfriend and honestly I'm in love with him. In addition, his relationship with Samantha was great. It developed realistically, properly, and slowly. Also, the issues they dealt with were <i>real.</i> I loved it all!<br /><br />Samantha as an MC... was well... I have no words? I don't really know what to say about her. She wasn't annoying, but not likable either. <b>She was just flat.</b> So I don't really care about her.<br /><br />If you're looking for a cute contemporary, I'd definitely recommend this one. Also, I decided to up my rating to a full 4 stars after writing this review, because it did clear more things for me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6845122725910053376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_252597141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252597141" />
    <a title="Sophia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3766576-sophia"><img alt="Sophia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571753231p2/3766576.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252597141?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/3766576-sophia">Sophia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252597141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17065969651370575672">I remember being super excited for this book because Katie from Katie's Book Blog compared the level of awesomeness to Anna and the French Kiss. And since AatFK is basically my favorite contemporary ever, you can imagine how high my expectation were. Which is why I was so sad when I started the book and felt... empty. I didn't connect well with Samantha. She seemed sort of detached to me. Her voice wasn't very strong in my head while I was reading and that made me lack invested emotions in the b</span>
  <span id="freeText17065969651370575672" style="display:none">I remember being super excited for this book because Katie from Katie's Book Blog compared the level of awesomeness to Anna and the French Kiss. And since AatFK is basically my favorite contemporary ever, you can imagine how high my expectation were. Which is why I was so sad when I started the book and felt... empty. I didn't connect well with Samantha. She seemed sort of detached to me. Her voice wasn't very strong in my head while I was reading and that made me lack invested emotions in the book. The first half of the book was almost boring to me, which left me so disappointed.<br /><br /> However, once the I got to page 280 or so, I got so absorbed into the story. The plot twist took me completely by surprise and I couldn't stop reading. I wondered why the whole book couldn't be like the last quarter. It was intense, emotional, and some scenes honestly brought tears to my eyes.<br /><br /> I felt like Jase and Samantha's relationship moved too fast, though I did believe there were genuine feelings for each other. I really like how they dealt with sex. It wasn't a split second decision in a hazy moment of lust. Instead, they talked about it and went shopping together for the necessary things, which was nice to read about.<br /><br /> Although the last quarter of the book was really amazing, the uneventful first half did detract from my enjoyment of the book. My Life Next Door is a wonderful debut that slowly simmers with the feelings of first love and questions the border between family and morals.<br /><br /> 3.5 keys.<br /><br />Sophia<br /> <a href="http://thebookbasement.blogspot.com/2012/11/my-life-next-door-by-huntley-fitzpatrick.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Basement</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17065969651370575672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_254764007" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254764007" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254764007?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of YA realistic fiction; 15+</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-read">lib-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=g-ya-realistic">g-ya-realistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=want-to-reread">want-to-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=quality-ya-fic">quality-ya-fic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254764007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16002552948365252916"><i>
  <b>My Life Next Door</b>
</i> is the kind of story that you expect to be light and fluffy . . . but then it surprises you.<br/>I thought this book would be very cliché: little rich girl falls for the boy next door; gets a whole new perspective on life through the eyes of a financially-strained, but very happy — unlike her own — family; and learns something big about herself over the course of one short summer. In a lot of ways, that is what this book is about. But, in truth, it is about so much more.<br/><br/>Samantha</span>
  <span id="freeText16002552948365252916" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>My Life Next Door</b>
</i> is the kind of story that you expect to be light and fluffy . . . but then it surprises you.<br />I thought this book would be very cliché: little rich girl falls for the boy next door; gets a whole new perspective on life through the eyes of a financially-strained, but very happy — unlike her own — family; and learns something big about herself over the course of one short summer. In a lot of ways, that is what this book is about. But, in truth, it is about so much more.<br /><br />Samantha Reed's character is, I think, one of the best — probably in the top ten, actually — YA heroines I've ever come across since I began reading YA fiction back in 2008. She stands up for herself and the people she cares about when it counts most, she thinks independently from her main influence in life — in this case, her mother — in a way that is smart and not just teenage rebellion. She is smart about sex choices, doesn't just jump into bed with the first boyfriend she gets — or even the third without some smart-shopping for Trojans (loved that scene!) — and is a generally well-rounded, intelligent young woman. I found being in Sam's head a very pleasant, refreshing, and, often times, spontaneously hilarious experience when compared to many of the female narrators of her genre. If Fitzpatrick's future heroines turn out to be even a tenth as good as Sam was, I'm in for a real treat.<br />And Jase . . . he is the kind of boy you'd want your daughter to marry. Truly. He's down to earth, loves his family, loves his animals (he's something of a zoo-keeper), and treats his girlfriend like gold. What's not to love? I think YA paranormal authors should take notes from Huntley Fitzpatrick on how to write a good male protagonist.<br />And Tim . . . I can't believe a debut author made me fall for a drug addict. Seriously. If the author decided to write a companion novel about Tim (maybe like Marchetta did with Thomas after Saving Francesca) and, hopefully, Alice, I'd be forever grateful to the Powers That Be.<br /><br />The bulk of this novel is about Samantha getting to know — and fall for — both Jase and his family. But towards the end, as the publisher-provided synopsis says, there is a big obstacle that is dropped on Sam's and the Garrett's heads, an obstacle that is not overcome easily. I wish there could have been a bit more resolution at the end with it <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Last we hear of Mr. Garrett is that he's out of ICU, and Sam's mom is still checking to see how he's doing; I would have liked for there to have been a coming-home-from-the-hospital scene, or at least a mention of a full recovery <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but as a whole I think the climax was handled well. <br />And, on a side note, can I just say how utterly <b>sexy</b> some of this book is? I wasn't expecting that, either, but I love surprises.<br /><br />Truly, I don't feel that my words can properly describe how much I loved this book, or how much I got out of it, or how much I wish more people would discover it and feel for it what I did. Does that mean this book was perfect? No, because no book is. But honestly, it was perfect for me. I'm extraordinarily pleased with it — so much so that I plan to reread it this summer — and will certainly be back for more from Fitzpatrick in future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16002552948365252916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_355932385" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10366996-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355932385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10511514905865449351">This book went from a 5-star read to a 1-star read. <br/><br/>I thought it would be about a romance. A contemporary novel that usually explores the values of family, friendship, life etc.<br/><br/>But by the end of the book...all I could think was, really? what was the point of all that drama?<br/><br/>There were so many unresolved issues <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[i.e. her friendship with Nan, what Tim would do, what was Sam's decision about moving, what would happen with her and Jace <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and it made me frustrated. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view s</a></span>
  <span id="freeText10511514905865449351" style="display:none">This book went from a 5-star read to a 1-star read. <br /><br />I thought it would be about a romance. A contemporary novel that usually explores the values of family, friendship, life etc.<br /><br />But by the end of the book...all I could think was, really? what was the point of all that drama?<br /><br />There were so many unresolved issues <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[i.e. her friendship with Nan, what Tim would do, what was Sam's decision about moving, what would happen with her and Jace <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and it made me frustrated. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Clay or Nan never got their comeuppance either. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I understand life like is like that sometimes, but for a book, there needs to be some sort of resolution. Especially you spend so many hours being invested in it. <br /><br />There's this big, bad event that happens, and I don't think it made the characters grow. If anything, we just get a lot of anxiety, sitting around and waiting for something to happen. When it does, it was anti-climatic. <br /><br />The romance didn't win me over either. Aside from their initial meet-up and the development of their relationship, the focus shifted. Jace is a sweet guy, but the romance didn't go anywhere. And perhaps it came a little too easily. <br /><br />The main character wasn't likable either. Till the very end, I couldn't decide if she was a good or bad person. She was described as having a perfect life, with perfect looks, perfect body, good grades and she's rich. But the main character fell flat for me, and there isn't much of an adjective I can use to describe her...except maybe vanilla. Bland. Perhaps cardboard. Definitely not memorable. <br /><br />Did I mention a whole of the book it's her working at her multiple jobs? Kind of boring. <br /><br />I'll mention that this book did have interesting secondary characters. The siblings Jace have are adorable such as George with his phobias. After a while, you get sick of all that dialogue though. It's like the author got too carried away and once again, it came down to not much really happening.<br /><br />No one learnt an amazing life lesson or repented. Nothing huge went down except that crazy, pointless twist. There wasn't a big conflict, the relationship between Sam and Jace was strong throughout the novel. Even when the 'ordeal' happened, there was this disbelief at how fast they went past that. Perhaps Jace is a little too perfect and fell flat too. He wasn't a realistic nor compelling character anymore. <br /><br />Overall, this book was a let down. </span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6pDHrg2xeG5Tmac88drUGT5+P6qEj8kLyVCXDgzjIy5sBThBSu4mbupohYV02PnJCGGpl7+JL97nt1ezvKJI5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4PtFHQn74YNrW4BRi48Cwj1ugyAl2ZzqYglQLF135npmbrryTqS/g9KqougOjS8SC3EVHR7fej9M7pCR7TaNsg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_18298225'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18298225-on-the-fence?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">On the Fence<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/5027236.Kasie_West?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Kasie West<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.05 avg rating &mdash; 49,044 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2014\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer12467337529624479895\">For sixteen-year-old Charlotte Reynolds, aka Charlie, being raised by a single dad and three older brothers has its perks. She can outrun, outscore, and outwit every boy she knows—including her longtime neighbor and honorary fourth brother, Braden. B<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12467337529624479895\" style=\"display:none\">For sixteen-year-old Charlotte Reynolds, aka Charlie, being raised by a single dad and three older brothers has its perks. She can outrun, outscore, and outwit every boy she knows—including her longtime neighbor and honorary fourth brother, Braden. But when it comes to being a girl, Charlie doesn\'t know the first thing about anything. So when she starts working at chichi boutique to pay off a speeding ticket, she finds herself in a strange new world of makeup, lacy skirts, and BeDazzlers. <span id="freeTextContainer14319284550263207775">Huntley Fitzpatrick grew up dreamy and distracted in coastal Connecticut. She flourished in a family of bookworms where everyone always had their nose in a book. She kept an exhaustively thorough journal which frightened her boyfriends but has proved very useful in her career as a writer. Her debut contemporary Romance, MY LIFE NEXT DOOR, was published in June of 2012 by Penguin-Dial for Young Rea</span>
  <span id="freeText14319284550263207775" style="display:none">Huntley Fitzpatrick grew up dreamy and distracted in coastal Connecticut. She flourished in a family of bookworms where everyone always had their nose in a book. She kept an exhaustively thorough journal which frightened her boyfriends but has proved very useful in her career as a writer. Her debut contemporary Romance, MY LIFE NEXT DOOR, was published in June of 2012 by Penguin-Dial for Young Readers. Now she laughs with and eavesdrops on her six children who provide her with perspective and material. She is represented by the amazing Christina Hogrebe of the Jane Rotrosen Agency.</span>
